# Comments for Question 1, LLM=Microsoft Phi-4

== Grader: Claude 3.7 Sonnet ==
  * grade_story_101.txt (grade=5.2)
    Clara's motivation to "reimagine the endings we fear" is established but lacks specificity about what endings she fears. Elias remains underdeveloped beyond being mysterious and supportive. The "weathered heart" attribute is told rather than shown through specific past experiences. Characters lack distinctive voices in dialogue.

  * grade_story_10.txt (grade=5.2)
    Arlen's character lacks depth beyond his "cheerless duelist" label. His motivation for seeking forgiveness feels underdeveloped and abstract rather than personal. While the connection to family recipes provides some backstory, we never learn what specific actions require forgiveness or why his dueling reputation matters. His transformation feels unearned without concrete examples of his flaws or meaningful character growth.

  * grade_story_1.txt (grade=4.2)
    The character's phobia-ridden nature is mentioned but never specifically explored. Eliot lacks distinctive voice and his stunt double profession is merely a label with no bearing on the plot. His motivation to "dance on the edge of madness" feels disconnected from his actions. The transformation described is told rather than shown, with vague statements about facing fears without specific examples.

  * grade_story_102.txt (grade=5.2)
    The "spineless" attribute is established but not fully explored. Finch's hesitancy and preference for shadows align with this trait, but his eventual determination contradicts it without sufficient development of this change. His motivation to decipher the prophecy lacks personal stakes, making his character feel more like a vehicle for the plot than a fully realized individual.

  * grade_story_105.txt (grade=5.2)
    The outcast scholar's motivation is clear but lacks depth. His "strangely trustworthy" attribute is mentioned but not demonstrated through actions. The character remains somewhat generic, with little distinctive voice or personality beyond his quest. His reaction to discovering the diaries feels predictable rather than revealing deeper character traits.

  * grade_story_0.txt (grade=5.2)
    Eliot's character is established with the "sheepish" and "analytically creative" traits, but these qualities aren't deeply explored. His motivation to charm the monster is stated rather than demonstrated through meaningful actions or internal conflict. While his use of the lamp shows some creativity, his personality lacks distinctive depth or complexity that would make him memorable. His dialogue is functional but not particularly revealing of character.

  * grade_story_108.txt (grade=4.2)

His motivation to "hush the madness" is clear but underdeveloped, and we never understand why he possesses this responsibility. The character remains a vehicle for plot rather than a fully realized individual with internal conflicts or growth.

  * grade_story_100.txt (grade=5.2)
